<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_31f01ef7-0f19-4842-8c15-853884869e02'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText15852569189605575166" style="display:none">"I need Owen to explain this. Because yes, I do know that Owen would never do that, but I also know Hannah would never lie about something like that."<br /><br />Mara and Owen are about as close as twins can get. So when Mara's friend Hannah accuses Owen of rape, Mara doesn't know what to think. Can the brother she loves really be guilty of such a violent crime? Torn between the family she loves and her own sense of right and wrong, Mara is feeling lost, and it doesn't help that things have been strained with her ex-girlfriend and best friend since childhood, Charlie.<br /><br />As Mara, Hannah, and Charlie navigate this new terrain, Mara must face a trauma from her own past and decide where Charlie fits in her future. With sensitivity and openness, this timely novel confronts the difficult questions surrounding consent, victim blaming, and sexual assault.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2307868156" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2307868156" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2307868156?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-ff">lgbtq-ff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2307868156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17238561079005598851"><strong>Girl Made of Stars</strong> is the kind of story that pinches and bites—unflinching and powerful. The kind of story that slits you open with the truth and leaves your heart bitter, afraid of everything, and angry at everyone, and so awful at holding all of it within your own skin that the tidal wave of your emotions threatens to drag you out to sea and drown you. The kind of story that leaves you in a trance after you’re finished. The one that just won’t let you go for days.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>So what is this book about?</u></b></span>
  <span id="freeText17238561079005598851" style="display:none"><strong>Girl Made of Stars</strong> is the kind of story that pinches and bites—unflinching and powerful. The kind of story that slits you open with the truth and leaves your heart bitter, afraid of everything, and angry at everyone, and so awful at holding all of it within your own skin that the tidal wave of your emotions threatens to drag you out to sea and drown you. The kind of story that leaves you in a trance after you’re finished. The one that just won’t let you go for days.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>So what is this book about?</u>
</b><br /><br />Mara, a bisexual high school junior, shares a bond strong enough to transcend words with her twin brother, Owen. When Owen is accused of raping his girlfriend—one of Mara’s best friends—the world as she knew it is left undone, those accusations turning into thorns snagging Mara’s skin and clothes and landing too heavy on her heart.<br /><br />Mara lingers at the intersection between believing her brother in his insistence on being innocent and always believing the survivor—her heart careening between the two and grasping at the words that would distill the truth down and weed out all the things that did not fit. Adding to the mottled mess of truth and lies in Mara’s head is her classmates and family, including her fiercely feminist mother, who publicly sided with Owen. Mara’s inner conflict is also threaded with the memory of her own past trauma—one that she’s never confessed and every time she tried to leave behind, it only caught fire and lit a dozen more.<br /><br />Around this tragedy runs an unrelenting plot that brings into sharp brutal relief a raw and unvarnished look at victim blaming, consent, male privilege and the tendencies of many to mock and underestimate a <em>pain</em> they haven’t endured. <strong>There is so much truth, pain and humanity in this book.</strong> I was nodding and marveling at the richness and poignancy of the author’s portrayal of such an important, devastating perspective on an all-too-timely subject. This is a book that truly digs in and exposes human selfishness, flaws, misconceptions, and tendencies—leaving questions that will land too hard for you to catch them. <br /><br /><strong>Girl Made of Stars</strong> is a powerful tale of betrayal and a vital primer on rape culture that will make you want to look away. But we can’t. If we don't look, we are just more people in the cyclical machine, keeping rape culture churning through our society. The closer we look, the more we see. It’s a story that provocatively and effectively illustrates how hopeless it may seem to fight something so vast and too terrifying to contemplate. How ridiculous it may seem to believe you can win—especially that what often follows such a tragedy is a prolonged, degrading, and oftentimes fruitless process. <br /><br />Mara’s moral struggle was indicative of how easy it can be to sink beneath the lie of what everyone else upholds and how difficult it can be to break free of that belief system which strangles everyone, and side with whom she truly believes in. But soon she realizes that sexual assault is not a ghost that would go silent if only you found the right way to quiet it, and eventually all that wondering, all that uncertainty gets crowded out, sharpening the truth of how little Mara knew her brother to account for all of him, and the cruciality of doing the<em> right</em> thing.<br /><br />It’s a book that hammers at the fact that neutrality has only ever helped the side of the oppressor, never the victim. We must always take sides. Silence encourages the tormentor, never the tormented. We are all accountable for what happens in our midst. <br /><br /><strong>Girl Made of Stars</strong> also highlights how being a survivor is being both other than and more than what everyone else will assume you are. That hope is a language you may still be learning – a thing you may stammer and halt through, but each day, you will find new words for “survivor” and they will shape your own name.<br /><br />But more than anything, it uncovers the brittle core of the truth which is that standing up for everyone else does not mean that all of them will stand up for you when you need someone. Not one of them would be the first one to defend you, but only because that spot is reserved for your name. You are the author and arbiter of your own recovery and every act of it will be a powerful declaration: “<em>I am on my side. Each day, I am more and more on my side.</em>”<br /><br />Also central to Mara's narrative is her relationship with Charlie, her (ex)girlfriend, who represents a nuanced, trailblazing depiction of a teen who identifies as non-binary. I love their relationship so much. I love how it was rooted in a deep, honest friendship of the unshakable kind, a friendship that could be busted nearly to breaking and come back stronger than before. I love how they acknowledged their flaws and how it affected their relationship and how they were both working on becoming better versions of themselves. It was all very authentic and raw and I really loved it.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren't asked, aren't believed, aren't considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return.</em>
  <br />
  <em>Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.” </em>
</blockquote><br /><br />Some books shape you in so many different ways. Some books change you so intrinsically that you couldn’t erase their influence on you anymore then you could change your DNA.<br /><br /><strong>Girl Made of Stars</strong> is one of those books.<br /><br /><b>TW:</b> rape, sexual assault, victim blaming, anxiety and panic attacks.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="17238561079005598851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1939700337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1939700337" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1939700337?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781328778239" href="/book/show/35721231-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2018">y-out2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-squads">favorite-squads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-arcs">x-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=she-did-that">she-did-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sapphic-books-shelf">sapphic-books-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2018">z-faves2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1939700337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6117313159957080331"><u>Feb. 13, 2019: A Note</u><br/>A month after I finished this book, on Valentine's day, a boy in my biology class who had been harassing me non-sexually for months told me he wanted to have sex with me. Today, an anonymous article was published by my school in which this was mentioned and discussed, under a pseudonym, and in which the experiences of a close friend were also shared - hers were far worse. And in a lot of ways I think I got off lucky, but seeing that article today felt like a punch in the gut</span>
  <span id="freeText6117313159957080331" style="display:none"><u>Feb. 13, 2019: A Note</u><br />A month after I finished this book, on Valentine's day, a boy in my biology class who had been harassing me non-sexually for months told me he wanted to have sex with me. Today, an anonymous article was published by my school in which this was mentioned and discussed, under a pseudonym, and in which the experiences of a close friend were also shared - hers were far worse. And in a lot of ways I think I got off lucky, but seeing that article today felt like a punch in the gut or maybe like flying, I don't know which one right now. And it's interesting because I've read a lot of books that touch on the experience of sexual assault and sexual harassment but this is the one that has come closest to capturing the feeling of taking back your body, and the experience of crying with your best friend who's been through something just as bad, and I read and reviewed this book before my experience but it still rings so so true. <br /><br /><u>Original Review</u><br />This is not a book I am worthy of reviewing. This is a masterpiece of human emotion, of writing, of character development. <br /><br />So <i>Girl Made of Stars</i> follows Mara, whose twin brother Owen has been accused of rape by Mara’s best friend. But it's... so much more than that. <b>
  <u>There is something about this book that just <i>hit</i> me.</u>
</b> I mean, it's kind of just perfect? The characters feel like completely real people, to a degree that is almost terrifying. The themes are perfectly handled. But most of all, this book just has a degree of <b>emotional authenticity</b> I have almost never seen in literature.<br /><br />There is a love triangle here with a bi lead, but it is handled <i>so well</i>. I think I might literally be known for hating this trope but this is the Most honest and open dynamic with a love triangle I have ever read. Mara’s dynamic with Charlie, her ex, is one of learning - they are two people who were best friends and then who fell in love and then who fell apart. And now Mara has to figure out why. Mara <i>also</i> has a relationship with a guy named Alex, one of Owen’s best friends - or maybe ex-best friends. Mara’s relationship with Alex is - vague spoilers - <i>not</i> the primary relationship of this book. But it’s also a fundamental part of Mara’s character development that I really like. And Alex is a very good person. I trust him.<br /><br />You know what I <i>really</i> love, though? MARA’S RELATIONSHIP WITH CHARLIE. Charlie is nonbinary [yes, she uses she/her pronouns] and is an incredibly complex character. But her relationship with Mara is the most top tier ting I’ve ever read. These two characters are both flawed, dealing with their own problems and desperately trying to figure themselves out. Their relationship makes me so happy and gives me so much hope. <br /><br />For me, the most important aspect of this book was <b>the narrative around Mara’s own trauma.</b> While this book is blurbed and described as a book about Hannah’s rape, it is also a story about the unspoken trauma so many young people face - <b>the trauma of having someone you trust violate you in a society that refuses to believe you.</b> The narrative treatment of rape is so fantastically done and important too, with so much weight given to Hannah's accusation yet so much nuance given to every character's feelings on what has gone down. Mara, Charlie, Hannah, Alex, and Mara's family have all lost someone they trusted, all in their own way, and <i>Girl Made of Stars knows</i> this. <br /><br />While <i>Girl Made of Stars</i> is not the most smoothly flowing, I somehow felt it actually made the book better? <b>Yes, this book is messy and complicated, but the world is messy and complicated too.</b> I think the nuanced characters and messy plot give this book its real feeling. I could not be happier to have read this book.<br /><br />I have... so much positive to say about this and literally nothing negative. I don’t think I’ve comprehensively explained why. I don’t think I am capable of that at this point in my life. But this book will be in my top five of the year. This is one of the best books I have read in my entire godforsaken life and I'm having one of my THIS I S SO B E A U T I F U L crises and. I don’t even know. None of you are allowed to publish books anymore, this book just killed all of them. And me too.<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a><br /><br /><b>➳➳ this is July's second mod pick for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/19432089-july-sapphic-squad-reads---into-the-drowning-deep-girl-made-of-stars" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sapphic Squad</a>, a book group I run with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-hiatus-queen" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaylin</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7706640-jamieson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jamieson</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42163117-emma" rel="nofollow noopener">Emma</a>! <i>I hope some of you will join us &lt;3</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6117313159957080331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2156328978" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2156328978" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2156328978?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781328778239" href="/book/show/35721231-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2156328978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3607667259810909167"><blockquote>
  <i>I can’t think about Owen. I can’t attach his name to Hannah on a hospital bed, bandages on her wrist, tears on her lovely face.</i>
</blockquote><br/>4 1/2 stars. I cried.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31351689.Girl_Made_of_Stars' title='Girl Made of Stars by Ashley Herring Blake' rel='nofollow noopener'>Girl Made of Stars</a> is about a situation that for the vast majority of us is not only horrifying, but unimaginable. For other feminists like me, our default is to offer compassion to rape survivors. To offer belief. To unite against the rapist. But... imagine if the alleged rapist was your closest friend, your anchor, the one person you've always </span>
  <span id="freeText3607667259810909167" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I can’t think about Owen. I can’t attach his name to Hannah on a hospital bed, bandages on her wrist, tears on her lovely face.</i>
</blockquote><br />4 1/2 stars. I cried.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31351689.Girl_Made_of_Stars" title="Girl Made of Stars by Ashley Herring Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Girl Made of Stars</a> is about a situation that for the vast majority of us is not only horrifying, but unimaginable. For other feminists like me, our default is to offer compassion to rape survivors. To offer belief. To unite against the rapist. But... imagine if the alleged rapist was your closest friend, your anchor, the one person you've always been able to trust. Imagine if it was your twin.<br /><br />This is the situation Mara finds herself in. She desperately wants to believe her brother when he says he did nothing wrong, but she knows the victim is not someone who is likely to lie. Torn between the feminist values she has always held close to her heart and her loyalty to her brother, Mara goes on an introspective journey that is ultimately about her own personal growth.<br /><br />Mara has a lot of issues of her own to deal with beyond this. At the start of the book she has just broken up with Charlie, who is genderqueer but uses female pronouns and still hasn't come out to her parents. The deeper reasons for the break-up are revealed as the novel progresses, tied in with Mara's reasons for being particularly affected by the accusation against her brother. <br /><br />It's a <b>hard-hitting critique of rape culture</b> and especially the ways victims are silenced by the disbelief of others. It's also an intimate portrait of a teenage girl's mind as she struggles to cope with her world being turned upside down, and figure out who she is at the same time. I think the book is stronger because it doesn't linger too long on Owen and the crime itself, choosing to focus instead on how Mara processes this impossible situation.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I’ve lumped myself in with my labels — girl, bi, queer — but I still can’t seem to really apply any of it to the person I see in the mirror every day. That girl is still voiceless, still scared.</i>
</blockquote><br />Mara's sexuality is neither stereotypical, nor the focal point of the book. We see her explore two relationships - with genderqueer, white Charlie and a Korean boy called Alex - but her liking of more than one gender is not treated as a big deal.<br /><br />In the end, this is a book about the damage caused when we treat rape survivors with suspicion. It is necessary for us to listen, even when we really don't want to.<br /><br />TW: Rape.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3607667259810909167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2434620306" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2434620306" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2434620306?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melanie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/68157476-may">may ➹</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2434620306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13196945107788158640"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534797953i/26166572._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren't asked, aren't believed, aren't considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return. Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Friends, I wish I could put this book into everyone in the entire world’s hands. This book is so powerful, so heartbreaking, so important, and just so beautifully crafted. But before I really even start this revi</span>
  <span id="freeText13196945107788158640" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534797953i/26166572._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren't asked, aren't believed, aren't considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return. Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Friends, I wish I could put this book into everyone in the entire world’s hands. This book is so powerful, so heartbreaking, so important, and just so beautifully crafted. But before I really even start this review, I want to preface that <b>this review is going to talk a lot about sexual assault.</b> And even though I implore you to pick up this book if you are able, this is a very dark book at times. Major <b>content and trigger warnings</b> for rape, sexual assault, physical abuse, pedophilia, bullying, depiction of grief, trauma, PTSD, and anxiety attacks. Another thing I want to touch on is that I was very surprised that this book surrounds two sexual assaults, not just the one you are originally led to believe. So, I don’t want any of you to be lulled into a sense of safety to only be hurt later on. <br><br><i>Girl Made of Stars</i> is a haunting book that I wish wasn’t so perfectly done. I wish this book wasn’t so realistic. I wish this book only made me cry because of the fictional content, and not because this is the actual world we live in. But in these pages, we follow a young girl named Mara whose brother is accused of raping one of her best friends. And we get to see how this rape impacts this entire friend group. Yet, we also get to see how it impacts Mara’s family, Mara’s school, and the entire community<br><br>➽ <b>Mara</b> - The star of this book. Mara is also bi and has panic attacks. <br>➽ <b>Owen</b> - Mara’s twin brother, who seems perfect and is very popular. <br>➽ <b>Charlie</b> - Realizing they are nonbinary, Mara’s best friend, and also Mara’s ex.<br>➽ <b>Alex</b> - Owen’s best friend, and Korean-American. <br>➽ <b>Hannah</b> - One of Mara and Charlie’s best friend, also Owen’s girlfriend. <br><br>Every 98 seconds, an American is sexually assaulted. 1 out of every 6 American women has been the victim of an attempted or completed rape in her lifetime. Only 310 out of every 1,000 sexual assaults are reported to police. out of 1,000 rapes, 994 perpetrators will walk free.*<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This. This is why I never said anything. Because no one ever believes the girl.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And we are teaching young girls to not speak up with our actions in this broken cycle of not believing them in a world that already chooses, over and over again, to not believe them. And it’s so fucking heartbreaking. It doesn’t matter if you’re in a relationship with the person. It doesn’t matter if you’ve had sex before. It doesn’t matter what you’re wearing. It doesn’t matter what you’ve said before. It doesn’t matter any circumstances; if it’s not consensual then it is rape. Rape culture is so real, so apparent, and so very much thriving in 2018. <br><br>You can love a person and still know and say that what they did was wrong. And this is a concept that we constantly cannot understand in this world. This book was extremely hard for me to read, because my brother is my best friend in this entire world, and imagining being in Mara's situation just completely gutted me over and over again. But loving someone doesn’t give them a free pass, and I think everyone needs to be reminded of that. If you say you will believe rape victims, then you have to believe all rape victims. You don’t get to pick and choose. And I beg you to start believing. And for anyone who needs it: I believe you. <br><br>Yet, this is a story about healing and reclaiming your body after it has been violated against your wishes. There is no right thing, no right amount of time, not even any correct word combinations that will help. Sexual assaulters take so much more from the victim that people realize, and it’s something that never goes away. But it can get better, and you have to do what is right for you, at your own pace. And this story really is a love letter to that. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Some parts of me are gone. Some others have come alive, woken by the need to fight, to matter, to be heard. Some parts are wary, others angry, others heartbroken. But I'm still me. I'm still moving.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book also does such a beautiful job talking about respecting people’s pronouns, gender, sexuality, and when and how they choose to come out, regardless of identities they’ve already came out about. Gender and sexuality can be so very fluid and always deserves to be respected. Everyone’s experiences are so very different, and only the individual knows what is best for them. <br><br>Overall, this was one of the hardest books for me to read all year, but I truly am so thankful that I was able to read it. I recommend this to anyone who is in the right headspace for it. And even though this was a hard book, it’s also really beautiful. I also loved the F/NB romance so very much in this one. Mara is one of my favorite characters in all of literature. And I will read every single thing Ashley Herring Blake writes forever. This is a heart-wrenching, flawless, masterpiece. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br>*Statistics from <a href="https://www.rainn.org/" rel="nofollow noopener">RAINN</a>. They are completely confidential, and available 24/7 if you need to talk to someone. Call 800.656.HOPE at any time. <br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52194039-shaina-cade" rel="nofollow noopener">Shai</a> at <a href="https://cadeunderbooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Cade Under Books</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/67405281-yusra" rel="nofollow noopener">Yusra</a>! ❤<br><br>❤ I also read this for <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/ContemporaryAThon?src=hash" rel="nofollow noopener">Contemporary-a-thon</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13196945107788158640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31027440-lala-booksandlala?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31027440-lala-booksandlala?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1860047305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17468981891871182906">flawlessly heart wrenching</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2056800133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2056800133" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2056800133?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781328778239" href="/book/show/35721231-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=tough-topics">tough-topics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=disability-and-mi">disability-and-mi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2056800133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6543983999620642008"><blockquote>
  <i>What else is there to do? What else is there for any girl to do, when everyone but her can forget everything like a random bad dream?</i>
</blockquote><br/>After breaking up with her girlfriend/best friend, Mara's greatest comfort comes from her twin brother, Owen - until her best friend accuses him of rape, and Mara's entire world is thrown into a whirlwind of confusion, heartbreak, and traumatic memories of her own.<br/><br/>Let me say, first of all, that this book is one of the most genuinely <b>
  <i>important</i>
</b> things I have </span>
  <span id="freeText6543983999620642008" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>What else is there to do? What else is there for any girl to do, when everyone but her can forget everything like a random bad dream?</i>
</blockquote><br />After breaking up with her girlfriend/best friend, Mara's greatest comfort comes from her twin brother, Owen - until her best friend accuses him of rape, and Mara's entire world is thrown into a whirlwind of confusion, heartbreak, and traumatic memories of her own.<br /><br />Let me say, first of all, that this book is one of the most genuinely <b>
  <i>important</i>
</b> things I have ever read in my life. The timing is perfect, with all of the sexual assault allegations filling the news media today, and it forces the reader to face a hard question: what do you do when someone you love is accused of rape?<br /> <br />→ <b>
  <i>mara</i>
</b> ←<br />Mara is such a lovable narrator, and so many of her feelings and thoughts were so incredibly candid and believable that it felt like she was a real person. She struggles from anxiety and panic attacks (which, as a person with an anxiety disorder, I felt were represented incredibly well), as well as PTSD.<br /><br />Watching Mara develop as she grows to listen to the victim and to consider that, just because she loves Owen, does not guarantee his innocence, was so incredibly sad but familiar. I, like many people, am ashamed to say that I have struggled at times in the past to believe a victim's account of an incident because I simply don't want to believe the individual in question could have done something so terrible. Mara shamelessly holds up a mirror for those times, before lighting a path leading to the realization that our loved ones are not always who we hope they will be.<br /><br />Despite the time it takes her to come to terms with the accusations, Mara never strays from being a caring young woman who wants desperately to take care of her loved ones.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Some parts of me are gone. Some others have come alive, woken by the need to fight, to matter, to be heard. Some parts are wary, others angry, others heartbroken. But I'm still me. I'm still moving.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>owen</i>
</b> ←<br />We are shown so many complex sides of Owen that I feel the story makes even the reader uncertain of the outcome at times. Owen is such a widely liked character, and is painted in such a wholesome light, that in the beginning of the book, it seems hard to imagine him as having intentionally done it. As the story progresses, and as Mara begins to see things differently, we are shown other perspectives of Owen - some so condemning that, in an instant, his entire persona shifts. I thought this was masterful storytelling on Ashley's part, and I loved how three-dimensional it made him.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Owen has always been loud and kind of crude with his friends, but that's not who he is with me. With me, he's a boy made of stars, soft and light and safe. He always has been.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>hannah</i>
</b> ←<br />Hannah is the innocent, sweet "hippie" of their friendship group, and she seems so wondrously in love with Owen that the segue into her accusations was downright jarring. Her likability only adds to the probability of her story, which realistically may make Mara's choice mildly easier than it would have been if Hannah had been an unknown, random character, or even an unlikable person. She was so delightful, though, and her heartache over having to make claims against Owen absolutely wrecked me.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I never got it before, you know? All the stories I've heard other women tell about how much shame there is in being the one it happens to. But there is. There's this weight of responsibility, of... god, I don't know. Of just existing."</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>charlie</i>
</b> ←<br />Beneath all of the rest of Mara's story, we have her ex-girlfriend and childhood bestie, Charlie, who Mara has broken up with because she feels incapable of carrying on a healthy relationship after her trauma. Charlie is a solidly flawed character, but never in a damning light, even when she reacts less-than-perfectly to Mara's painful history. She offers a terrific look into the life of a nonbinary character, and the struggles she faces in her daily life with her identity. <i>(Obviously, as a cis-gendered woman, I can't speak to the authenticity of this rep, so while I enjoyed it, I am always open to reading own-voice reviews on this aspect!)</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I'm not sure. Both? Neither? Something else altogether?"</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>bisexuality</i>
</b> ←<br />While the book has an enjoyable range of diversity in its casting, the most prominent aspect of that diversity was Mara's own bisexuality. Not only does she spend a sizable portion of the story struggling with her feelings for her ex-girlfriend, she also plays with the option of a male partner. I won't spoil who the individual is, but it opens up some incredible conversations regarding consent, sex, and her openness to people regardless of gender identity or sexuality.<br /><br />As a bi woman who is also less on the love for "two genders" end of the spectrum and more on the "two <i>or more</i> identities" end, I adored every moment of the bi rep in this book. Much like in Ashley's last YA release, <i>How to Make a Wish,</i> she puts emotions and explanations into words that are so profound and resonating that they brought tears to my eyes. She doesn't shy away from discussing the struggles that come with biphobia specifically, even from misunderstanding loved ones.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>And hey, that's more than a lot of kids get, especially in the South, where going out in public as a queer person can be like tiptoeing through a minefield.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>other noteworthy topics</i>
</b> ←<br />A few other things I wanted to touch on:<br /><br />•	In the beginning, we hear stories of how Mara and Owen’s mother considers herself a devout feminist, but as the story progresses, we see her gradually shift further away from her values in order to defend her son. This was such an incredibly candid view on how <i>hard</i> it can be for someone to admit that their loved ones have done something harmful, despite the morals they typically adhere to.<br /><br />•	Empowerment through sexuality is addressed in scenes where Mara chooses to dress in revealing clothing in order to draw attention away from another character’s pain; though her motives are wholesome, she finds that she loves the way the attention makes her feel, and makes a note that, when consent is given, being shown sexual attraction from other parties can be empowering and fun.<br /><br />•	In one scene, two characters are participating in some pretty heavy petting, and consent is directly <b>
  <i>asked for;</i>
</b> one character even comments on how incredibly sexy and empowered she feels for being asked and saying “yes”. Later, consent is revoked during sexual activity, and the opposite party is immediately apologetic, understanding, and drops the issue. <b>This is exactly the kind of consent discussion that YA books need!</b><br /><br />→ <b>
  <i>final thoughts</i>
</b> ←<br />I know this review is longer than my typical posts, but there are so many incredible and important moments in this story, and I've only shown you the tip of the iceberg. Ashley Herring Blake is doing work that most YA authors aren't brave enough to carry out, and she is executing it flawlessly. She has earned herself a permanent spot on my favorite authors list, and I only hope that this release will get the attention it deserves. I hope with everything in me that you will take my words to heart and pre-order yourself a copy of <i>Girl Made of Stars</i>. You won't regret it.<br /><br /><b>Content warnings:</b> sexual assault, biphobia, homophobia, anxiety, depression, PTSD.<br /><br /><i>All quotes are taken from an unfinished ARC and may differ from final publication. Thank you so much to HMH Books for Young Readers for providing me with an ARC in exchange for my honest review, and thank you so much to Ashley Herring Blake for doing such profound and important work in the YA literary field.</i><br /><br />You can find this review and more <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2017/12/08/girl-made-of-stars/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> on my blog!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6543983999620642008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2233854107?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2233854107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer750431419675606358">This story stirred my heart. <br/><br/>I absolutely needed to read it when I learned it was about a girl whose twin brother is accused of sexually assaulting his girlfriend at a party. It sounds like such an impossible situation. Who do you believe? Your brother, who you’ve known since before you were born, or his girlfriend, who is also your friend?<br/><br/>The reason why this story moved me so much is because it was very realistic and Ashley Herring Blake has a beautiful lyrical writing style that can bring you </span>
  <span id="freeText750431419675606358" style="display:none">This story stirred my heart. <br /><br />I absolutely needed to read it when I learned it was about a girl whose twin brother is accused of sexually assaulting his girlfriend at a party. It sounds like such an impossible situation. Who do you believe? Your brother, who you’ve known since before you were born, or his girlfriend, who is also your friend?<br /><br />The reason why this story moved me so much is because it was very realistic and Ashley Herring Blake has a beautiful lyrical writing style that can bring you to tears in less than a second. <br /><br />This is an important book. The author discusses consent, sexual assault as well as identity in such a meaningful and honest manner. Some scenes physically hurt. The world is an imperfect place where teenagers act in cruel ways and don’t always realize how much their actions can hurt the other person. Like Mara, I became angry at the boys and girls calling Hannah names and wanted to defend her in any way possible. <br /><br />The author makes it clear that we have to talk about these awful situations. Of course, admitting to being raped is something that takes a lot of courage, and as we know, in some cases the accusations against the rapist are not even taken seriously or proven. But whether or not we are believed, it’s still important to speak up because keeping it all in can be more detrimental. <br /><br />Fine book. Now, however, I require a fluffy read. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="750431419675606358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2062411998" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2062411998" />
    <a title="may ➹" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68157476-may"><img alt="may ➹" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538949856p2/68157476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2062411998?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ➹" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ➹" href="/user/show/68157476-may">may ➹</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781328778239" href="/book/show/35721231-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-female">pov-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=my-heart">my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-1st">pov-1st</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=my-soul-hurts">my-soul-hurts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=tears">tears</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2062411998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12649477550554228661">Me, thinking about this book at any moment in my life:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525923595ra/25514632.gif' width='300' height='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren’t asked, aren’t believed, aren’t considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return.<br/><br/>Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>This book destroyed me.</b> This book destroyed me and it destroyed the chances of all other books this year because I have no doubt that this will be one of my favorite boo</span>
  <span id="freeText12649477550554228661" style="display:none">Me, thinking about this book at any moment in my life:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525923595ra/25514632.gif" width="300" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren’t asked, aren’t believed, aren’t considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return.<br><br>Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>This book destroyed me.</b> This book destroyed me and it destroyed the chances of all other books this year because I have no doubt that this will be one of my favorite books of the year, if not my MOST favorite.<br><br>Let me put it this way: I haven’t cried over a book since 2016. This book made me sob. I teared up so many times. And then I reread the book <i>two days</i> after I first read it.<br><br>I don’t cry over books!! Tears do not stay on my face for the whole last half of books!! And I certainly don’t reread books <i>two days</i> after I first read them!!!! This book is a big deal.<br><br><b>I just… have no words about how much this book affected me.</b> It’s so beautiful and poignant and gorgeously written and I can’t wait for everyone to read it, because it is 10000% worth it. Even if you feel like you’re dying inside.<br><br>First of all, this story is really, really heavy. It talks about rape and other forms of sexual abuse, also tackling issues of victim-blaming, sexuality, gender identity, and more. So it’s no surprise that this is a hard-hitting book. And it’s not just hard-hitting. It’s like… shoving and pushing on you all at once. It’s really intense, but it’s intense in a way that makes it so good, and powerful, and meaningful.<br><br>This book follows the story of Mara, whose twin brother Owen is accused of raping her best friend, Hannah. It’s about learning who to believe in and what to believe in. It’s about facing the past and figuring out how that will shape you in the future. But most of all, <b>it’s a story about healing from things that you never thought you could get back up from</b>.<br><br>Mara is our main character, a girl who is trying to recover from the past while dealing with the present, and wondering what it means for the future. The way her thoughts and emotions are written is so RAW, and <b>it’s just so beautiful to see her finding her way up from the bottom of an abyss she never thought she could escape</b>. Her arc (and pretty much every character’s arc in this book) is written and developed so well, whether it’s her learning how to live with the trauma she’s faced but not let it rule her, or her learning how to deal with a twin brother who has done something horrific.<br><br>This book relies a lot on character development—another reason why I fell so deeply in love with it—and all the side characters are written just as beautifully as Mara:<br><br><blockquote>☼ Owen is portrayed as a boy who’s trying to reconcile with what he’s done, but his actions are never excused. This is the brother that Mara has loved her whole life, but she has to accept that someone so close to her can do something so horrendous.<br><br>☼ Hannah is a girl devastated by what’s been done to her by Owen, and <b>what’s continually being done to her as a society that will never believe her</b>, but what’s also evident is her growth and her strength and her ability to keep getting up even when everything brings her down. There is one scene between Mara and Hannah that made me SOB, because of how powerful and empowering it was.<br><br>☼ And finally, Charlie (Mara’s ex in the beginning to something else at the end) is a genderqueer character who uses she/her pronouns, who is struggling to really define herself and trying to find the bravery to express herself in a way that she needs to. I connected so much to Charlie and her struggles that it literally made me cry.</blockquote><br>Mara and Charlie’s relationship is honestly so, so beautiful. (Also a reminder not to call this f/f because even though Charlie uses she/her pronouns, she is genderqueer and not a girl!!!) <b>It’s about learning to come to terms with their own identities, but also learning how to support each other at the same time.</b> It means a lot to me for a lot of personal reasons.<br><br>God. It’s been months since I read this, but I still can’t summon enough words to talk about this book. Mostly because 1) I’m still destroyed and trying to work through my feelings over this, but also because 2) this book is about flawed people working through their flaws, and yet it is written almost <i>flawlessly</i>.<br><br>Just... please read this book. It is one of the most powerful, deeply touching, well-written books I’ve ever read, and it means so much to me beyond the fact that it made me cry. It is just <i>beautiful</i> and <i>stunning</i> and an honest-to-god love story to every single person who is <b>discovering who they are, how they fit into society, and learning to love whoever they turn out to be</b>.<br><br><b>:: rep ::</b> bisexual female MC with anxiety, sapphic genderqueer LI, Korean male LI<br><b>:: content warnings ::</b> rape, sexual abuse and assault, anxiety/panic attacks<br><br><blockquote>
<i>Thank you to Houghton Mifflin Harcourt for the review copy in exchange for an honest review! This did not my affect my opinions in any way.</i> <i>All quotes are from an advanced copy and may differ in final publication.</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12649477550554228661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer18065200101988900005">i had a difficult time rating this. if there was ever an argument for half star ratings, it would be this book. i found my mind saying 4 stars while my heart was saying 3. and heres why. <br/><br/>on the positive side of things, the writing was beyond beautiful. and i really liked the title, even more so once i read how it plays into the story. i am sucker for books where the main characters are boy-girl twins. i really wish i had a boy twin, myself. and so learning about how mara was ‘a girl made of star</span>
  <span id="freeText18065200101988900005" style="display:none">i had a difficult time rating this. if there was ever an argument for half star ratings, it would be this book. i found my mind saying 4 stars while my heart was saying 3. and heres why. <br /><br />on the positive side of things, the writing was beyond beautiful. and i really liked the title, even more so once i read how it plays into the story. i am sucker for books where the main characters are boy-girl twins. i really wish i had a boy twin, myself. and so learning about how mara was ‘a girl made of stars’ and how it played into the relationship with her brother was really rewarding. <br /><br />but on the negative side, i just could not find any deeper emotions to give. yes, i understand how heartbreaking this situation is and i get that situations like happen more often than they should, but i just found myself not really emotionally invested in this story. i hope that doesnt make me a bad person, because stories like this are so important and need to be told/represented, but i felt very unaffected whilst reading this. which is not what you want with a book like this.<br /><br />so im conflicted. this was a good book, but i was really wanting more from it. however, i think this is a book everyone should read just because of its message alone.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>3.5 stars</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_2443274487" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2443274487" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2443274487?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2443274487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12016688880062915558"><b>
  <i>4.5 Poignant, Emotional & Thought-Provoking Stars for Girl Made of Stars!</i>
</b><br/><br/>This book was beautifully written. Rape, abuse, and sexuality are not easy topics. Blake did an amazing job of telling this all too important story. <b>It was told with hope, love and healing.</b> It doesn't sugar coat life after abuse. <i>Yet, it was powerful in its message that victims are worth the telling. That despite a culture that often places blame on the victim they are worth believing. That there are people who will lis</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12016688880062915558" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>4.5 Poignant, Emotional &amp; Thought-Provoking Stars for Girl Made of Stars!</i>
</b><br /><br />This book was beautifully written. Rape, abuse, and sexuality are not easy topics. Blake did an amazing job of telling this all too important story. <b>It was told with hope, love and healing.</b> It doesn't sugar coat life after abuse. <i>Yet, it was powerful in its message that victims are worth the telling. That despite a culture that often places blame on the victim they are worth believing. That there are people who will listen. That they are not simply victims - they are survivors.</i><br /><br />This is the story of Mara. Mara is such a complex character. There was simply no way I could not adore her. She was both broken and brave, scared and strong. Mara is struggling with trauma. A secret she has kept for years that is eating away at her. It causes panic attacks, PTSD and anxiety. <b>The silence, shame and trauma she suffered were heart wrenching to read about.</b><br /><br />Mara is a twin. Mara &amp; Owen are as close as twins can be. That makes it all the more complex when one of her best friends, Hannah, accuses Owen of rape. Hannah and Owen were dating. They had been sexually intimate in the past. Hannah said no, in the heat of things. Owen didn't stop. What I truly appreciated was that Blake didn't sugar coat how difficult this was for Mara. She struggled with her belief. This was her brother. <i>How this rape affected her family, her friendships and ultimately her own truth were written with such honesty and vulnerability that it made my heart ache.</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Some parts of me are gone. Some others have come alive, woken by the need to fight, to matter, to be heard. Some parts are wary, others angry, others heartbroken. But I'm still me. I'm still moving. We all are, in some way or another."</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>This is YA that transcends its label. It's a book that should be read, experienced and felt by all ages and genders.</b></span>

<div id="review_2287457593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2287457593" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2287457593?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=to-buy">to-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=slump-worthy">slump-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=recommend">recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=best-contemporaries">best-contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2287457593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer263098383699046456">I don’t really know how to review this, or even rate it. I just know that everyone in the world should probably read this book.<br/><br/>My memory of it is not fresh (read it five months ago; shoutout to my renowned timely reviews), and even when it was I was rendered pretty speechless. Basically what I’m saying is that there are so many thoughtful reviews of this and mine will very much pale in comparison. <br/><br/>So what it comes down to is: you should read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1939700337?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elise’s review</a>, or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2434620306?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melanie’s</a>, and then if you want to </span>
  <span id="freeText263098383699046456" style="display:none">I don’t really know how to review this, or even rate it. I just know that everyone in the world should probably read this book.<br /><br />My memory of it is not fresh (read it five months ago; shoutout to my renowned timely reviews), and even when it was I was rendered pretty speechless. Basically what I’m saying is that there are so many thoughtful reviews of this and mine will very much pale in comparison. <br /><br />So what it comes down to is: you should read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1939700337?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Elise’s review</a>, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2434620306?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Melanie’s</a>, and then if you want to watch someone struggle to write complex outdated faded emotions they didn’t even understand in the first place, journey on back over here!<br /><br />Now that that’s out of the way: let’s do some sections.<br /><br /><br /><b>SYNOPSIS</b><br /><br />Mara’s best friend is her twin, Owen - until his girlfriend and her friend, Hannah, accuses him of rape. Faced with choosing between her own sense of morality and standing with her family, Mara struggles to do the right thing.<br /><br />And also her ex-girlfriend is there.<br /><br /><br /><b>THINGS ABOUT THIS BOOK THAT ARE BETTER THAN THEY HAVE ANY RIGHT TO BE</b><br /><br />This book is approximately ninety-nine point nine percent five star ratings (and don’t @ me - I go to a college that doesn’t offer math). There’s a good reason for that. This book covers so many complexities of an unbelievably sensitive issue with deftness and wiseness and skill rarely seen in YA.<br /><br />There is a “but,” but it’s coming later.<br /><br />This story deconstructs the concept of “type of girl.” It covers means of healing that aren’t necessary quiet, or nonviolent, or quick or easy or simple but are unbearably, achingly real. It shows there is no such thing as a completely bad person, while steering clear of stating that people aren’t capable of completely bad actions.<br /><br />Basically, this book realizes something that YA novels rarely do: that a complicated topic requires a complicated story. There are easier ways to cover sexual assault. None of them involve siblings or friendships or even intoxication or belief or morality. The simplest stories say “this is consent, and here we believe women.” And those stories are fine, and they bring awareness, but that’s not what’s real.<br /><br />This book is mercilessly, unrelentingly real.<br /><br />Which is why it sucks so bad that it didn’t click for me.<br /><br /><br /><b>IT’S NOT YOU, PRETTY BOOK, IT’S ME</b><br /><br />I stand by all the dramatic proclamations I’ve made about this so far. I think this is by far the best rendering of the complicated nature of sexual assault that I’ve read. However.<br /><br />On a personal level, as a story with characters and a world, it didn’t work for me.<br /><br />It’s mostly whatever, because everything that is so good about this book is capable of transcending normal book stuff. But I can’t really click with a book without clicking with the characters??? (Also: how many times can I use the word “book” in one paragraph. Book book book book book.)<br /><br />Anyway. That’s the story for why this book didn’t make me feel much of anything, and I’m sticking to it.<br /><br />Mara has a pretty wonderful development arc in this, but she’s just about the only character I feel like I halfway understand. And even she felt flat sometimes and it’s her!!! story!!!! From her perspective!!! And everyone else was even worse.<br /><br />Also, I thought this book was trying to do too much. A lot of this was spent on Mara thinking about her relationship with her now ex-girlfriend, Charlie, and I just...didn’t care. It felt so much less meaningful than the main story, and every time we divulged into this B-plot I was just annoyed it was taking time away from the main focus.<br /><br />Because, as mentioned, this book is overwhelmingly complicated. So trying to add more to that was unnecessary and, honestly, kind of annoying and distracting.<br /><br />What it comes down to, really, is that as a book in the typical sense this didn’t work for me. Luckily, this is more than a book - and the more-than-a-book stuff worked.<br /><br />Bottom line: Is this an unpopular opinion????<br /><br />----------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />i haven't the FOGGIEST idea what to rate this book, which might be one of the most important ones i've ever read.<br /><br />so.<br /><br />review <i>and</i> rating to come, i guess.<br /><br />----------<br /><br />EVERYTHING HURTS AND I CAN'T STOP READING</span>
  <a data-text-id="263098383699046456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
