<div id="review_2492425812" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2492425812" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2492425812?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2492425812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15991746012491643877">Powerful, emotional, and thought-provoking, Ashley Herring Blake's <b>
  <i>Girl Made of Stars</i>
</b> is a beautifully written, poignant book about the bonds of family and friendship, gender and sexual identity, the emotional traumas faced by victims of sexual abuse and assault (not to mention the "blame the victim" mentality which is all too prevalent), and the confusion and anxiety which often accompanies love. <br/><br/>This was utterly phenomenal.<br/><br/>"Once upon a time...a brother and sister lived with the stars. They</span>
  <span id="freeText15991746012491643877" style="display:none">Powerful, emotional, and thought-provoking, Ashley Herring Blake's <b>
  <i>Girl Made of Stars</i>
</b> is a beautifully written, poignant book about the bonds of family and friendship, gender and sexual identity, the emotional traumas faced by victims of sexual abuse and assault (not to mention the "blame the victim" mentality which is all too prevalent), and the confusion and anxiety which often accompanies love. <br /><br />This was utterly phenomenal.<br /><br />"Once upon a time...a brother and sister lived with the stars. They were happy and had wild adventures exploring the sky."<br /><br />Mara and Owen are twins, so similar and yet so different from one another, yet they are incredibly close. But one night following a big high school party, Owen's girlfriend Hannah (who is also one of Mara's best friends) accuses Owen of raping her. How could someone Mara once shared a womb with, someone she knows better than anyone else, have done such a thing? Even as their parents rally around Owen and declare his innocence, can Mara believe her brother is truly innocent? If not, what does that do to their relationship? And if so, what happens to her friendship with Hannah?<br /><br />Confused, hurt, and angry at so many people after the incident, Mara feels adrift because her relationship with her ex-girlfriend Charlie is tremendously uncertain. She knows she wants to be with Charlie but is afraid of what that means, afraid of letting someone get too close. But more than that, Mara has been able to keep a traumatic event in her own life a secret, but at what cost? If she speaks up, will anyone believe her? Will her parents believe her? Or will she be treated by her peers, her friends, her family in the same way Hannah has been?<br /><br />"What else is there to do? What else is there for any girl to do, when everyone but her can just forget everything like a random bad dream? I have no idea what <i>moving on</i> sounds like, looks like. I've spent the past three years trying and decidedly not getting over anything."<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Girl Made of Stars</i>
</b> doesn't exist in a fantasy world where every person who does wrong is punished, and everyone learns from their mistakes. It's a book that accepts that life is often grey rather than simply black and white, but we can't stop fighting for what is right, fighting to make sure those who do wrong are punished. I think that's why this book works so well—it's never heavy-handed or preachy, but it does emphasize the difference between acceptable and unacceptable behavior.<br /><br />Ashley Herring Blake is amazingly talented. Her ear for dialogue, her eye for evocative imagery, the flawed yet unforgettable characters all dazzled. One of the greatest compliments I can give is that this book felt a little like one of Jandy Nelson's exquisite books, two of my absolute favorites (<b>
  <i>I'll Give You the Sun</i>
</b> and <b>
  <i>The Sky is Everywhere</i>
</b>), yet she is an author with a style all her own.<br /><br />Like many YA books—and like life, honestly—there are moments in this book in which you wish the characters would just say what they were feeling rather than avoid the truth. But while those moments may cause frustration they are realistic, particularly given the issues that these characters are confronting, so it didn't detract from my enjoyment of this book.<br /><br />Beautiful, emotional, and thought-provoking. I couldn't ask for anything more! <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>, or check out my list of the best books I read in 2017 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15991746012491643877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2417093149" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2417093149" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2417093149?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=heroines-i-adore">heroines-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=i-just-have-a-lot-of-feelings">i-just-have-a-lot-of-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=masterpiece">masterpiece</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=oh-my-god-marry-me">oh-my-god-marry-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=the-gay-agenda">the-gay-agenda</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=2018-faves">2018-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2417093149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1479518150516972730"><blockquote>
  <i>Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren’t asked, aren’t believed, aren’t considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return.<br/><br/>Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>TW:</b> Sexual assault and rape. Readers should especially take caution with Chapter Eighteen, especially those of you who have had your own experiences, because it was very difficult to read.<br/><br/>I can't remember the last time I sh</span>
  <span id="freeText1479518150516972730" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren’t asked, aren’t believed, aren’t considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return.<br /><br />Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>TW:</b> Sexual assault and rape. Readers should especially take caution with Chapter Eighteen, especially those of you who have had your own experiences, because it was very difficult to read.<br /><br />I can't remember the last time I shed so many tears over a book. I wasn't even halfway through with this one and they were already rolling down my cheeks in abundance. That is <i>very</i> rare for me, because normally it would take at least nearing the end for a story or its characters to elicit a strong emotional reaction out of me, let alone straight up <i>tears</i>. But with this one, I can't even tell you how many moments choked me up.<br /><br />I jumped into this book without reading the blurb, so I went into it having no idea what it was going to be about. As soon as I saw the story unfold, I was immediately invested. The way this book is written and the way these events were treated was just so beautifully and realistically done. I genuinely felt horrible for Mara because of the impossible dilemma she had to face, causing her to question everything about her own twin brother who she was supposed to love unconditionally. I also felt for Hannah and my heart shattered for her when she felt the need to apologize, as if any of this was her fault.<br /><br />This book poses that question that many of us would never dare to answer; if someone in your family that you love dearly was accused of such a heinous act, would you still stand by them no matter what? Even if the odds seem very likely that they may have really done said act? Would you blindly support them and sit idly by while they kept spreading lies and blamed the person they took advantage of and victimized? Would you do all of that simply because they're family?<br /><br />We normally wouldn't even want to think about these things, but this book tackles this very subject in a way that was achingly realistic. The way Mara's feminist mother was so quick to bury herself in denial and stand by her son no matter what, even if perhaps somewhere deep down she knew that there were holes in his story. She wouldn't even entertain the possibility of her own son committing such a horrible thing. The fact that Mara herself <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[had been a victim of sexual assault in her past <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> which ultimately made this whole situation even worse for her. It was just so well-done and so <i>heart-wrenching</i>. <br /><br />And that's not the only thing this book tackles. It also touches on slut-shaming, sexuality and gender identity. All of these were also handled extremely well. Hell, there was even somewhat of a love triangle in this book and even THAT worked, because it wasn't the contrived, pandering kind of love triangle we often see in YA. You know a book is amazing when even something like a freaking love triangle is portrayed in a realistic way that made sense.<br /><br />That's really why I adore this book, the unflinching realism of it. I was sort of worried going in that it would be a little too flowery or lyrical, kind of like those contemporary books that are written as if they're magical realism books, but this one is just completely raw and honest and accurate, with just a dash of lyrical prose here and there that added to its beauty. The overall message and the serious themes being explored never got weighed down by the prose, they worked beautifully together.<br /><br />Of course the subject matter of this book is frustrating, especially in this post-Weinstein era we live in and the growing of the #MeToo movement, but this book managed to voice all of those frustrations and call out these issues in such a poignant, HONEST way. This is probably one of the most important books I've ever read and will no doubt make it into my end of the year list. <br /><br />This is a book that everyone should read and talk about and hand over all the awards to. Ashley Herring Blake has created a masterpiece.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1479518150516972730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2429213591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2429213591" />
    <a title="alana ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12402009-alana"><img alt="alana ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599221603p2/12402009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2429213591?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alana ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alana ♡" href="/user/show/12402009-alana">alana ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781328778239" href="/book/show/35721231-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=tough-topics">tough-topics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2429213591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10074739254626766534">Ladies and gentlemen, this is the reason why I will never stop reading YA books. This book made me feel like I was drowning and given one second to come up for air before being shoved back under the water. It was so raw and intense that at times I had a lump in my throat from trying not to cry and scream for Hannah and Mara. To put it simply this book hurts but <strong>
  it is so very important
</strong>.<br/><br/>Initially, I was very hesitant to pick this up because let's be real, this is not any easy topic to read abo</span>
  <span id="freeText10074739254626766534" style="display:none">Ladies and gentlemen, this is the reason why I will never stop reading YA books. This book made me feel like I was drowning and given one second to come up for air before being shoved back under the water. It was so raw and intense that at times I had a lump in my throat from trying not to cry and scream for Hannah and Mara. To put it simply this book hurts but <strong>
  it is so very important
</strong>.<br /><br />Initially, I was very hesitant to pick this up because let's be real, this is not any easy topic to read about. You know it's going to be a heavy book based on the synopsis alone, but I was also hesitant because if this book was not handled and written the way it was it could have come off as extremely offensive and an utter disaster. Thankfully, it was not and will definitely go down as one of my favorite reads of 2018 and probably one of my favorite books of all time.<br /><br />Mara, oh, Mara. Where do I being with her? I absolutely loved everything about her. She's such a lovable character who felt so real while reading this. Her growth was absolutely amazing throughout this story. Mara suffers from PTSD, anxiety, and panic attacks due to a prior sexual assault incident, and my heart <strong>ACHED</strong> for her. When Mara's twin brother, who is her entire world, is accused of raping her best friend it's no surprise that Mara struggles greatly with this for various reasons. How could her brother possibly do something so heinous? But how can she not believe her best friend? Especially when Mara's family is so quick to stand behind Owen. And so begins Mara's story of realizing that sometimes our loved ones are not who we hoped they would be and coming out the dark place she kept herself in for the last three years.<br /><br />I want to keep this review short because this book just demands to be felt and read. I don't think any review could ever do justice for how powerful <em>Girl Made of Stars</em> actually is. But before I wrap it up there are a few things I want to add that you can expect from this story also. The first is dealing with gender identities. I'm not sure that I've ever read a book dealing with this before and while I do have to admit that I am not the most familiar with some of the terms that are used regarding gender identities in today's society I am always working on educating myself. So I felt this was a great start. The second is bi-sexuality rep, which I thought was handled extremely well and branched off into other important topics like consent. The third is strong female friendships, you all know I'm a sucker for them and this was no exception.<br /><br />All in all, I can't remember the last time I've read a book that evoked so many emotions from me. This story is powerful, raw, honest, heart-breaking, and gut wrenching all in one, but it's also a story about survival and finding your voice which is so important in the society we live in today. There are not enough stars in the world I could give this book. There are not enough rooftops I could shout off of telling you to read this book, just do it. Your heart will hurt, you'll cry, you'll want to scream, but this book is absolutely worth the pain.<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishchicksblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookishchick" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishchick_/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10074739254626766534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6564226498948308255">I feel wrung out emotionally after reading this. This was my first Ashley Herring Blake novel, and I’m going to pick up her other books as soon as I can. Her writing was beautiful and strong. She handled such a devastating topic really well, and in a way that was realistic, brutal, and yet hopeful. </span>

<div id="review_2305376965" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305376965" />
    <a title="Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword"><img alt="Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603584262p2/28146945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305376965?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword" href="/user/show/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword">Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781328778239" href="/book/show/35721231-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=best-book-dedications">best-book-dedications</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=made-me-angry">made-me-angry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=edge-of-my-sit">edge-of-my-sit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=my-cinammon-rolls">my-cinammon-rolls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=quote-material">quote-material</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305376965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6729368061885709384">✪✪✪✪✪<br/><b>After reading this book I have become a girl made of pain.</b><br/>➽<u>
  <b>FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED</b>
</u><br/><br/> Find this review and more content in my blog, <a href='https://inkismysword.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ink Is My Sword</a><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren't asked, aren't believed, aren't considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return.<br/>Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1545958242i/26820064.jpg' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <i>All images were found on Pinterest, I do not own any of them.</i>
</blockquote><br/>⚠</span>
  <span id="freeText6729368061885709384" style="display:none">✪✪✪✪✪<br><b>After reading this book I have become a girl made of pain.</b><br>➽<u>
  <b>FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED</b>
</u><br><br> Find this review and more content in my blog, <a href="https://inkismysword.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ink Is My Sword</a><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren't asked, aren't believed, aren't considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return.<br>Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.”</i>
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1545958242i/26820064.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <i>All images were found on Pinterest, I do not own any of them.</i>
</blockquote><br>⚠ rape, sexual assault, panic attacks<br>💬<br>When everyone I know gives a book 5 stars there is a small part of me wanting to defy the normal and be different, here is the thing there is NO way I could do that in this case.<b> This book is a heart-breaking masterpiece, rating stars are not enough to encapsulate all my feelings and thoughts for this book</b>. The journey of reading this novel was so nerve-wracking and hurtful, I truly cannot understand how the author was able to finish it, I certainly applaud it. <br><br>The concept of the story screams <b> please proceed with caution</b>. I mean it could have been a shit show. The idea of telling the story of the twin of the perpetrator, and at the same time best friend of the victim, its genius. When reading headlines in the news, it is easy to forget all the people involved are humans. Humans with emotional links to others, humans with family, humans who are flawed but also loved. <b>In this book, is easily shown how painful and hard can be to accept that someone you knew was not what you thought they were.</b>. <br><br>A story that weights pounds was compacted in a 200 something page book, <i>perfectly</i>. For a contemporary, the story flowed without slumps of boredom, or to-slow sections. Every chapter, every scene something was happening. <b>Ashely wrote the story where it kept giving turns and putting me in the edge of my seat holding a breath (I knew I was holding)</b>. The actions Mara took at the end, the constant peace to conflict moods, almost made me rip all my hair. It's a book that never makes you disengage, it demands your 100%.<br><br>I wish I could reach into the page and hug every single character, even the bad ones.<br><br>★<b>Mara:</b><br><br>I loved how real and flawed her character was. It was realistic for her to be so conflicted when confronting both of her favourite people. I loved to see how Ashley showed rape does not only affect the victim but also others. Mara kept surprising me by the end of the novel, she confronted her past in ways I wasn’t expecting, but I was glad I was watching it unfold. <i> I wish I could give her a hug to let her know I understand how hard everything is, and how brave she is for confronting everything and trying to be fair with the morality of things. </i> <br><br>★<b>Charlie:</b><br>I am not gonna lie I am completely biased when I say, I loved Charlie. Charlie is the epitome of <i>my type</i>. They are artistic, creative and a great person. I loved how they were there for Mara even if they were supporting Hannah. Can I just please marry you? <br>I do wanna address the pronoun issue I saw in some reviews. We did got a scene were Charlie told Mara they didn’t mind if they were called her, so I do not have a huge issue with the narration. YET I would have preferred Mara referred to Charlie as them at least in her thought processing and when talking to them. <i> I wish I could give Charlie a hug saying how they are valid and how their parents are gonna love them anyway. And that they deserve all the love, especially mine.</i><br><br>★<b>Alex:</b><br>He is a cinnamon roll, who plays the violin. He had a lot in his shoulders as well, one of the things I loved the most about his characterization was the freedom he had to show emotions. We got multiple scenes of him sobbing and although it made me sad for him I also was happy to see male characters crying, BECAUSE IT'S NORMAL. <i>I wish to hug Alex and tell him everything was gonna be okay. </i><br><br>★<b>Hannah:</b><br>She was definitely a character I wish I got more insight too. I know why we didn’t, as the story is more focused on Mara, but Hannah plays a huge role in all of it. I wasn’t able to connect as much I wanted, I really wish we got a sequel following Hannah with the aftermaths. <i> I wish I could hear and tell her I am sorry for all the evil in this world and remind her of how strong she still is. </i><br><br>★<b>Owen:</b><br>UGH, but also I feel a bit for you. He definitely messed up and I couldn’t stop myself to feel for him a bit when he was nice to Mara yet the rumours he spread when he knew he had been at fault made me not redeem him at all.  I wish to hug him just to see if it would break his wall to make him realize how bad he screwed up. <br><br>★<b>Parents:</b><br>Not going to lie I wanted to slap Mara’s mom so hard. Ups, but really. She is a perfect example of a person who fights and stands for rights when nothing affects them, yet when they are involved everything is different. <i> I wanna hug her because I know how painful her position must be, but at the same time directly slap her after letting go. </i><br><br>For a book with such a heavy topic in focus, I was surprised to still be engaged in different relationships. Charlie and Mara, made my heart beat wildly. Mara and Alex made me tear some. <br><br><b>C+M </b><br>Of course, the main relationship in the book. I have a soft spot for their connection because they started as friends and then evolved to more, it’s definitely one of my favourites romantic tropes. I loved the angst and how they were still trying to make their friendship survive after their break up. Although this book hs a very sad undertone, my belly felt butterflies in some scenes between both of them. <br><br><b>M+A</b><br>I am guessing many of you don’t consider what happened between Mara and Alex a relationship even, but I took it as a bond made by tragedy and need to share the pain. I loved this depiction of physical and emotional need. It felt raw and real, and I was surprised by how well I took them not being an actual couple. <br><br><b>Rape</b>. This is a difficult theme to cover, is so easy to not handle it with care or just using it as a plot device, but I found Ashley explored a whole new side of this terrible thing. We get to see how difficult can rape become for all the people surrounding the people involved. I was very glad to see the play of the grey lines between the black and white fo things. The fact that Owen is not a villain completely strange to us made everything more difficult to swallow. Yes, I was mad there wasn't exactly justice meet, but I appreciated the realness it gave to everything. <br><br>😻Everything.<br>😾Nothing.<br><br><b>My Christmas wish is for more people to pick this book up.</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“It’s changed me forever, but changed doesn’t have to mean broken.”</i>
</blockquote><br>📢<br><b>Recommendation</b>. If you like hard-hitting contemporaries then you will enjoy this book. <br><br>💭<b>Pre-reading thoughts</b>: <br>Finally getting to one of the most hyped books by my GR friends. <br>I hope this book doesn't break me too much. <br>Buddy-read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/48727754-chandler-ainsley" rel="nofollow noopener">my queen and now youtube superstar🌺 </a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6729368061885709384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2511512976" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2511512976" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2511512976?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35900742-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2511512976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2366015490251974137">Library Young Adult ebook...<br/> excellent discussion pick! <br/> <br/>“Sweetie, this will blow over. It’s a misunderstanding. You know your brother”.<br/> “You keep saying that”.<br/> “Saying what?”.<br/> “That it’s a misunderstanding. That I know Owen. But...Mom, I know Hannah, too”.<br/><br/>“What do we do?” What’s going to happen to Owen? And Hannah... we can’t just not listen to her. You’ve always said that we have to listen to girls no matter—“<br/> “He’s ours, Mara, Mom says, a kind of quiet fury edging her words. He’s my son. And </span>
  <span id="freeText2366015490251974137" style="display:none">Library Young Adult ebook...<br /> excellent discussion pick! <br /> <br />“Sweetie, this will blow over. It’s a misunderstanding. You know your brother”.<br /> “You keep saying that”.<br /> “Saying what?”.<br /> “That it’s a misunderstanding. That I know Owen. But...Mom, I know Hannah, too”.<br /><br />“What do we do?” What’s going to happen to Owen? And Hannah... we can’t just not listen to her. You’ve always said that we have to listen to girls no matter—“<br /> “He’s ours, Mara, Mom says, a kind of quiet fury edging her words. He’s my son. And we love him. That’s what we do”. <br /><br />Mara feels numb. Mom is kinda freaking out. Dad... well.... he is kinda comatose...<br />Mara’s twin brother, Owen is accused of raping Mara’s best friend, Hannah. <br /><br />As I followed this story... I paused early on and tried to imagine myself in the shoes of any one of these characters. After finishing this novel I was simply frozen for several minutes. I wasn’t sure what I ‘thought’ ...but I definitely ‘felt’ sad. <br /><br />Many minutes later— I painfully appreciated what the author set out to do - and accomplished.<br />Punching- gut powerful ending! Satisfying? Readers can decide....<br />Truthful? ... ‘pretty much’!!!<br /><br />Mara had a close relationship with her twin brother, Owen. <br />She had seen him crude with his friends, but he was never that way with her. With her,<br />“he’s a boy made of stars, soft and light and safe”. <br /><br />Mom use to tell them stories at bedtime about the two of them - twins born in June- soaring through the sky.<br /> “Once upon a time, a brother and sister lived with the stars. They were happy and had wild adventures exploring the sky...”<br /><br />Home is so cozy when little with those bedtime stories....<br />then enter ‘𝐋𝐢𝐟𝐞’ out in the world....less cozy. <br /><br />I kept thinking about the title of the book: “Girl Made of Stars”....<br />Not TWINS made of stars....<br />So?? I wondered... what was coming down the pipes? And why ‘this’ specific title? <br />Made perfect sense after I finished reading it. <br /><br />For Mara...there were too many unsaid things in her life to say anything at all....<br />how she felt about her brother - her family- herself. She was splitting in two -scared constantly. <br />Recurring nightmares about losing her voice happened at least once a week. She had haunting unexpressed memories. Mara will be forced to face her own past ...not a pretty picture with no easy solutions. <br /><br />The author dives smack in the middle of the complexities of our closest relationships — presenting us with gut-wrenching issues to examine: haunting lessons about how gentle folks we love and trust can be capable of great brutalities. <br /><br />Relevant important issues inside this Teen-Gem..with an ending not easy to forget and think about long after. <br /><br />Well written- completely engaging! I’m glad I read it.<br /><br />Thanks to Larry H. His review inspired me yesterday and our library had it available. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2366015490251974137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2136669848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136669848" />
    <a title="Sophie Elaina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54237690-sophie-elaina"><img alt="Sophie Elaina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572297086p2/54237690.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136669848?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie Elaina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie Elaina" href="/user/show/54237690-sophie-elaina">Sophie Elaina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781328778239" href="/book/show/35721231-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=owned-hardcovers">owned-hardcovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=owned-e-arcs">owned-e-arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136669848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9514868083203249472">This book is truly fantastic! Its such an important, relevant and heart-breaking read, and the author wrote it in both a beautiful and shockingly real way. It's seriously one of the best books I’ve ever read! I'm going to try my hardest to do it justice in this review, but honestly I don't know if that's even possible because there aren't enough words that exist to describe my feelings towards it.<br/><br/>The book follows Mara; one half of Mara and Owen, inseparable twins that have always been close. So </span>
  <span id="freeText9514868083203249472" style="display:none">This book is truly fantastic! Its such an important, relevant and heart-breaking read, and the author wrote it in both a beautiful and shockingly real way. It's seriously one of the best books I’ve ever read! I'm going to try my hardest to do it justice in this review, but honestly I don't know if that's even possible because there aren't enough words that exist to describe my feelings towards it.<br /><br />The book follows Mara; one half of Mara and Owen, inseparable twins that have always been close. So when Hannah one of Mara's closest friends accuses Owen of rape, Mara is torn on who to believe out of two people she loves and has always trusted. Split between being loyal to her family and her own sense of truth she begins to feel overwhelmingly lost. Making the trauma from her own past come rolling back, she must face her the past and look to her future. She begins seeking comfort in her brother's best friend Alex and her ex-girlfriend Charlie hoping to make sense of her own feelings and everything that she has lost.<br /><br />“Even girls made of stars are captives, bound at the wrists and traded like property. Even girls made of stars aren’t asked, aren’t believed, aren’t considered worth the effort unless they can offer something in return.<br />Even girls made of stars buy into those lies sometimes.”<br /><br />This book confronts many difficult topics, including questions surrounding consent, victim blaming, and sexual assault. And while being sensitive to the subject matter the author managed to broach it in a very open way that didn't shy away from things that need to be questioned more in society.<br /><br />"I never got it before, you know? All the stories I've heard other women tell about how much shame there is in being the one it happens to. But there is. There's this weight of responsibility, of... god, I don't know. Of just existing."<br /><br />Along with the very heavy topics the book is an own voices novel with bisexual representation. And there is also a genderqueer love interest. Which were both excellent to see since I haven't seen nearly enough of this kind of representation in young adult literature. I was very happy to see how amazingly diverse the novel was and how well written each individual character was. Even though I can't relate on a personal level to this specific story, I do find it very exciting to see more and more diversity and the fact that no matter who you are there are books out there with characters going through the same things as me or you. There are even side plot lines in this book exploring anxiety, ptsd, panic attacks, depression, sexism, biphobia, homophobia and bullying. And it was great to see these things brought to light and addressed, however if you do find sensitive subject matter triggering I would keep in mind that the topics aren't brought up in a subtle way. <br /><br />"Owen has always been loud and kind of crude with his friends, but that's not who he is with me. With me, he's a boy made of stars, soft and light and safe. He always has been."<br /><br />There wasn't much in terms of romance, since the main character had recently broken up with her girlfriend just prior to the beginning of the novel. But the overall character development was extremely well done. And the relationships and friendships in general were very original and honestly not the usual type of thing you see in young adult contemporary. <br /><br />"Some parts of me are gone. Some others have come alive, woken by the need to fight, to matter, to be heard. Some parts are wary, others angry, others heartbroken. But I'm still me. I'm still moving."<br /><br />Overall this book was wonderful and I can't get passed how amazingly well done the novel is. I will definitely be looking into Ashley Herring Blake's past and future works. And I highly recommend you pick up this book, it's a read you don't want to miss. The subjects that are brought to light are so relevant and it's important we keep fighting to change the norm and support this kind of development when it comes to literature. The truth is, that this kind of literature is a ground breaking step in the right direction. If you couldn't already tell, the thing I loved most about this was the representation, but I need to mention it one more time because it is honestly outstanding, and there is even more things that I've not brought up for spoiler reasons. But first and foremost this is a story about survival, the ways in which people deal with trauma, and the endurance of heart-breaking truths.<br /><br />THANK YOU SO MUCH to Netgalley, Houghton Mifflin Harcourt Children's Book Group, and Ashley Herring Blake for giving me the chance to read this stunning book in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />For more reviews + bookish content, check out my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.sophieelaina.com/">https://www.sophieelaina.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9514868083203249472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10901233825886957585"><a href='http://catsandpaperbacks.wordpress.com/2017/11/02/earc-review-girl-made-of-stars-by-ashley-herring-blake/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review also on my blog</a><br/><br/><a href='http://www.twitter.com/catspaperbacks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a><br/><br/><a href='http://www.instagram.com/catsandpaperbacks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookstagram</a><br/><br/><b>I received an arc from the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</b><br/><br/>I read How to Make a Wish a few months ago and absolutely loved it and I was excited to see the author was coming out with more. Like her previous book, Girl Made of Stars deals with a heavy issue, that being rape. And unlike previous books that deal with rape or sexual assault, that being the rapist is the main character's brother. Not even just her brother but her twin br</span>
  <span id="freeText10901233825886957585" style="display:none"><a href="http://catsandpaperbacks.wordpress.com/2017/11/02/earc-review-girl-made-of-stars-by-ashley-herring-blake/" rel="nofollow noopener">Review also on my blog</a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.twitter.com/catspaperbacks" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.instagram.com/catsandpaperbacks" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookstagram</a><br /><br /><b>I received an arc from the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</b><br /><br />I read How to Make a Wish a few months ago and absolutely loved it and I was excited to see the author was coming out with more. Like her previous book, Girl Made of Stars deals with a heavy issue, that being rape. And unlike previous books that deal with rape or sexual assault, that being the rapist is the main character's brother. Not even just her brother but her twin brother.<br /><br />The book approaches the subject less with "oh she must be lying" but instead with Mara having a difficult time to grapple with the truth of it. But no resentment is held towards Hannah at any times. Although Mara's parents sided with her brother Owen immediately.<br /><br />I really liked Mara as a character and that she has a feminist magazine she runs at her school. At a point she protests against the strict and sexist dress code.<br /><br />There were also themes of romance but it was minimal. She and her friend Charlie had a romance before the book began and had broken up. Charlie is genderqueer and there is discussion around that and her fear of coming out to her parents. It's great to see a book where a non-binary character was the love interest.<br /><br />Overall, it was a great book and dealt with a difficult subject well.</span>

<div id="review_2073378923" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073378923" />
    <a title="Romie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33510193-romie"><img alt="Romie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579037929p2/33510193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2073378923?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Romie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Romie" href="/user/show/33510193-romie">Romie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781328778239" href="/book/show/35721231-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=2018-releases">2018-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=favourites-2018">favourites-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=bi-mc">bi-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=queer-books">queer-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2073378923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6148983689762470311"><i>“But if I’m made of stars, then where am I? Where’s the real me?”</i><br/><br/>This book broke me. It physically hurt to read it. It was so painful I cried most of the time. But it was worthy every single tear. So worth it.<br/><br/>This is a story that needed to be told, needed to be heard, needed to be read. This is the story of Mara, and how she discovered that her twin brother, her favourite person on this earth, the person she considers her other half, raped one of her best friends, Hannah. This is a story about l</span>
  <span id="freeText6148983689762470311" style="display:none"><i>“But if I’m made of stars, then where am I? Where’s the real me?”</i><br /><br />This book broke me. It physically hurt to read it. It was so painful I cried most of the time. But it was worthy every single tear. So worth it.<br /><br />This is a story that needed to be told, needed to be heard, needed to be read. This is the story of Mara, and how she discovered that her twin brother, her favourite person on this earth, the person she considers her other half, raped one of her best friends, Hannah. This is a story about loving two people so much you want to believe them both, because it hurts to much to think one of them is telling the truth, and the other one is lying. This isn’t the story of a monster who did something to the good girl, this is the story of an ordinary human, not evil but not angel either, who took something from another human being. This is the story of a sister trying to deal with this on her own, because she broke up with the person she loved the most and she can’t even tell her why, because it’s too close to what’s happening to their friend.<br /><br />There is an important discussion on feminism all throughout this book. Mara and Owen’s mom says she is a feminist, and yet when her own son is accused of having raped someone, she never, not even once, wonders if maybe her son actually did it. She never considers that Hannah might be telling the truth. So what, people consider themselves a feminist, but when something happens to their family, then it’s bye to their conviction? Being feminist doesn’t mean being one just when it’s convenient, it means you believe the victims, always, with no what ifs and shit. You believe them.<br /><br />I found Mara extremely strong and brave, because after the shock, after having went through her own thoughts and sorting them out, she doesn’t just do nothing, she acts. Mara is this incredible bi girl, in love with marvelous genderqueer Charlie, and even times are hard and it’s hella scary to be her, she acts. She cannot just do nothing. It’s not her. It’s not what it means to be feminist, to be an activist. She’s lost in her own life, but she doesn’t let that take away from her her power to act. Mara’s insecurities are important to this book, what happened to her, the fact that she was sexually assaulted is important to this book. She is powerful, what happened to her didn’t take this from her.<br /><br /><i>We’re both wearing skirts. Not so short that Principal Carr could find any violation, but short enough to raise an eyebrow.<br />It’s such a little thing, this skirt. For other girls, maybe it’s makeup or a sport or having sex or not having sex or writing or music or kicking ass in school or wearing your hair so it looks like the sun’s unruly rays. I think every girl has a thing or two, tiny details in her life that say <b>This is me. I’m done hiding. I’m done feeling ashamed.</b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6148983689762470311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amitaf0208" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amitaf0208" href="/user/show/13531666-amitaf0208">Amitaf0208</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13531666-amitaf0208?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2494687925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12021695163416684731">5 bright stars for the Girl Made of Stars. What a thought-provoking book. It dealt with a difficult subject in a way that did not alienate the reader. Loved all the characters especially Mara. Good read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2287074041" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47273713-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443055563p2/47273713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2287074041?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/47273713-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781328778239" href="/book/show/35721231-girl-made-of-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47273713-anna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47273713-anna?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47273713-anna?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47273713-anna?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2287074041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5143916627990586181">For such a good concept, this was so disappointing. <br/><br/>None of the characters elicited any connection from me. Mara irritated me most of the way through (I had a reason for this when I finished it last night but I didn't write it down so naturally I've forgotten it by now, oops). Charlie was kind of a shitty friend but we're expected to like her, which no. Not to mention Mara and Charlie's relationship didn't seem all that healthy?? Mara was so stressed over everything with Charlie and they had thi</span>
  <span id="freeText5143916627990586181" style="display:none">For such a good concept, this was so disappointing. <br /><br />None of the characters elicited any connection from me. Mara irritated me most of the way through (I had a reason for this when I finished it last night but I didn't write it down so naturally I've forgotten it by now, oops). Charlie was kind of a shitty friend but we're expected to like her, which no. Not to mention Mara and Charlie's relationship didn't seem all that healthy?? Mara was so stressed over everything with Charlie and they had this on-again-off-again thing going on, which obviously isn't good for moving on. Hannah as a person was alright, I didn't mind her, but the constant description of her hair as tangled, wild and mane-like is in direct clash with the emphasis on how pretty her hair is. That makes no sense. No one looks good with a rat's nest. Don't lie to me. Not a big deal, just kind of weird. <br /><br />Owen was supposed to be a good, loving brother who did something horrible but he was presented as your stereotypical sexist dick the entire book. When the premise involves him being a complicated, two-sided character, making him only a bad dude ruins it. It was terrible character writing.<br /><br />The writing in general wasn't good either. It was pretentious at times and preachy-sounding at others. Overall, it kind of sucked. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Finally, the moral of the book is belief in rape cases is easy: always believe the victim (Mara literally says always believe the girl no matter what, but the author did include a resource specifically for male victims in the note at the end, so I'll give her the benefit of the doubt on this one). The book is supposed to be about how difficult and complicated this stuff is, but in the end it wants you to believe that it's actually not complicated at all. The direct clash here pissed me off and made this so much less impactful than it could have been. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="5143916627990586181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_40495957'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40495957-heartstopper"><img alt="Heartstopper: Volume One (Heartstopper, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1541887843l/40495957._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PmhRKeVt1vTq01+wTh4MZGeO/ohyogqk2vZDXZexZyMs9Vxwx7mKyNjlVPPfOVcFczdPZKEPxqBNR6oY/rwRrg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kA5om+mOVR051+APJ/+y9216DO7Z1OZuS7kbLKYkoQOCk2XCy1oJIQvh60y22OmWecO9Agp5KmrcCPJpzynXjg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8545130.Ashley_Herring_Blake">About Ashley Herring Blake</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8545130.Ashley_Herring_Blake"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1593803118p3/8545130.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8545130.Ashley_Herring_Blake">Ashley Herring Blake
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,017
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15171878832451480914">Ashley Herring Blake is a reader, writer, and mom to two boisterous boys. She holds a Master’s degree in teaching and loves coffee, arranging her books by color, and cold weather. She is the author of the young adult novels Suffer Love, How to Make a Wish, and Girl Made of Stars (Houghton Mifflin Harcourt), and the middle grade novels Ivy Aberdeen’s Letter to the World and The Mighty Heart of Sunn</span>
  <span id="freeText15171878832451480914" style="display:none">Ashley Herring Blake is a reader, writer, and mom to two boisterous boys. She holds a Master’s degree in teaching and loves coffee, arranging her books by color, and cold weather. She is the author of the young adult novels Suffer Love, How to Make a Wish, and Girl Made of Stars (Houghton Mifflin Harcourt), and the middle grade novels Ivy Aberdeen’s Letter to the World and The Mighty Heart of Sunny St. James. Ivy Aberdeen’s Letter to the World was a Stonewall Honor Book, as well as a Kirkus, School Library Journal, NYPL, and NPR Best Book of 2018. Her YA novel Girl Made of Stars was a Lambda Literary Award finalist. You can find her on Twitter and Instagram at @ashleyhblake and on the web at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ashleyherringblake.com">www.ashleyherringblake.com</a>. She lives in Georgia.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15171878832451480914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
